        <script nonce="c403aa25d63bef2aeaf98fa7983e5a2c">
            var state = { mapper_id: 1 }
            var s_current_url = new URL(document.URL)
            var s_urlParams = new URLSearchParams(s_current_url.search)
            var isOrganicSearch = true
            if (s_urlParams.has("utm_source") || s_urlParams.has("wpsrc")) {
                isOrganicSearch = false
            }
            if (isOrganicSearch) {
                switch (document.referrer) {
                    case "https://www.google.com/":
                        var wpsrc = "Google Organic Search"
                        break
                    case "https://search.yahoo.com/":
                        var wpsrc = "Yahoo Organic Search"
                        break
                    case "https://www.bing.com/":
                        var wpsrc = "Bing Organic Search"
                        break
                    default:
                        break
                }
                if (wpsrc) {
                    s_urlParams.append("wpsrc", wpsrc)
                    window.history.replaceState(
                        state,
                        document.title,
                        s_current_url.origin + s_current_url.pathname + "?" + s_urlParams.toString()
                    )
                }
            }
        </script>

/* Document
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * 1. Correct the line height in all browsers.
 * 2. Prevent adjustments of font size after orientation changes in iOS.
 */

html {
  line-height: 1.15; /* 1 */
  -webkit-text-size-adjust: 100%; /* 2 */
}

/* Sections
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * Remove the margin in all browsers.
 */

body {
  margin: 0;
}

/**
 * Render the `main` element consistently in IE.
 */

main {
  display: block;
}

/**
 * Correct the font size and margin on `h1` elements within `section` and
 * `article` contexts in Chrome, Firefox, and Safari.
 */

h1 {
  font-size: 2em;
  margin: 0.67em 0;
}

/* Grouping content
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * 1. Add the correct box sizing in Firefox.
 * 2. Show the overflow in Edge and IE.
 */

hr {
  box-sizing: content-box; /* 1 */
  height: 0; /* 1 */
  overflow: visible; /* 2 */
}

/**
 * 1. Correct the inheritance and scaling of font size in all browsers.
 * 2. Correct the odd `em` font sizing in all browsers.
 */

pre {
  font-family: monospace, monospace; /* 1 */
  font-size: 1em; /* 2 */
}

/* Text-level semantics
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * Remove the gray background on active links in IE 10.
 */

a {
  background-color: transparent;
}

/**
 * 1. Remove the bottom border in Chrome 57-
 * 2. Add the correct text decoration in Chrome, Edge, IE, Opera, and Safari.
 */

abbr[title] {
  border-bottom: none; /* 1 */
  text-decoration: underline; /* 2 */
  text-decoration: underline dotted; /* 2 */
}

/**
 * Add the correct font weight in Chrome, Edge, and Safari.
 */

b,
strong {
  font-weight: bolder;
}

/**
 * 1. Correct the inheritance and scaling of font size in all browsers.
 * 2. Correct the odd `em` font sizing in all browsers.
 */

code,
kbd,
samp {
  font-family: monospace, monospace; /* 1 */
  font-size: 1em; /* 2 */
}

/**
 * Add the correct font size in all browsers.
 */

small {
  font-size: 80%;
}

/**
 * Prevent `sub` and `sup` elements from affecting the line height in
 * all browsers.
 */

sub,
sup {
  font-size: 75%;
  line-height: 0;
  position: relative;
  vertical-align: baseline;
}

sub {
  bottom: -0.25em;
}

sup {
  top: -0.5em;
}

/* Embedded content
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * Remove the border on images inside links in IE 10.
 */

img {
  border-style: none;
}

/* Forms
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * 1. Change the font styles in all browsers.
 * 2. Remove the margin in Firefox and Safari.
 */

button,
input,
optgroup,
select,
textarea {
  font-family: inherit; /* 1 */
  font-size: 100%; /* 1 */
  line-height: 1.15; /* 1 */
  margin: 0; /* 2 */
}

/**
 * Show the overflow in IE.
 * 1. Show the overflow in Edge.
 */

button,
input { /* 1 */
  overflow: visible;
}

/**
 * Remove the inheritance of text transform in Edge, Firefox, and IE.
 * 1. Remove the inheritance of text transform in Firefox.
 */

button,
select { /* 1 */
  text-transform: none;
}

/**
 * Correct the inability to style clickable types in iOS and Safari.
 */

button,
[type="button"],
[type="reset"],
[type="submit"] {
  -webkit-appearance: button;
}

/**
 * Remove the inner border and padding in Firefox.
 */

button::-moz-focus-inner,
[type="button"]::-moz-focus-inner,
[type="reset"]::-moz-focus-inner,
[type="submit"]::-moz-focus-inner {
  border-style: none;
  padding: 0;
}

/**
 * Restore the focus styles unset by the previous rule.
 */

button:-moz-focusring,
[type="button"]:-moz-focusring,
[type="reset"]:-moz-focusring,
[type="submit"]:-moz-focusring {
  outline: 1px dotted ButtonText;
}

/**
 * Correct the padding in Firefox.
 */

fieldset {
  padding: 0.35em 0.75em 0.625em;
}

/**
 * 1. Correct the text wrapping in Edge and IE.
 * 2. Correct the color inheritance from `fieldset` elements in IE.
 * 3. Remove the padding so developers are not caught out when they zero out
 *    `fieldset` elements in all browsers.
 */

legend {
  box-sizing: border-box; /* 1 */
  color: inherit; /* 2 */
  display: table; /* 1 */
  max-width: 100%; /* 1 */
  padding: 0; /* 3 */
  white-space: normal; /* 1 */
}

/**
 * Add the correct vertical alignment in Chrome, Firefox, and Opera.
 */

progress {
  vertical-align: baseline;
}

/**
 * Remove the default vertical scrollbar in IE 10+.
 */

textarea {
  overflow: auto;
}

/**
 * 1. Add the correct box sizing in IE 10.
 * 2. Remove the padding in IE 10.
 */

[type="checkbox"],
[type="radio"] {
  box-sizing: border-box; /* 1 */
  padding: 0; /* 2 */
}

/**
 * Correct the cursor style of increment and decrement buttons in Chrome.
 */

[type="number"]::-webkit-inner-spin-button,
[type="number"]::-webkit-outer-spin-button {
  height: auto;
}

/**
 * 1. Correct the odd appearance in Chrome and Safari.
 * 2. Correct the outline style in Safari.
 */

[type="search"] {
  -webkit-appearance: textfield; /* 1 */
  outline-offset: -2px; /* 2 */
}

/**
 * Remove the inner padding in Chrome and Safari on macOS.
 */

[type="search"]::-webkit-search-decoration {
  -webkit-appearance: none;
}

/**
 * 1. Correct the inability to style clickable types in iOS and Safari.
 * 2. Change font properties to `inherit` in Safari.
 */

::-webkit-file-upload-button {
  -webkit-appearance: button; /* 1 */
  font: inherit; /* 2 */
}

/* Interactive
   ========================================================================== */

/*
 * Add the correct display in Edge, IE 10+, and Firefox.
 */

details {
  display: block;
}

/*
 * Add the correct display in all browsers.
 */

summary {
  display: list-item;
}

/* Misc
   ========================================================================== */

/**
 * Add the correct display in IE 10+.
 */

template {
  display: none;
}

/**
 * Add the correct display in IE 10.
 */

[hidden] {
  display: none;
}

conditions</u></div><div> and </div><div class="textTertiary xSmallRegular" data-testid="link"><u>Privacy policy</u></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div><div><img src="https://onemg.gumlet.io/a_ignore,w_360,h_208,c_fit,q_auto,f_auto/kc51gsyjlfij2barujbc.jpg" class="Disease__overviewImage__QVIKz ImageLoader__img-loaded__wfU_q" alt="Hair loss" title="Hair loss"/><div class="container-fluid widget-container"><div class="col-6 marginTop-8"><div class="flex alignCenter justifyBetween"><h1 class="l1SemiBold">Hair loss</h1></div><div class="marginTop-16 flex alignCenter"><img src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/2000/svg&quot; viewBox=&quot;0 0 0 0&quot;%3E%3C/svg%3E" class="Avatar__avatar__Gga63 Avatar__imageBoxMedium__CJemM Avatar__loadingAvatar__c5OTg" alt=""/><div class="flexColumn ContentPageTitle__marginLeft8__IhR5_"><span class="smallRegular textSecondary">Written By<!-- --> <a href="https://www.1mg.com/editorial-policy-processes/dr.-sakshi-sharma-16" class="smallMedium noAnchorColor ContentPageTitle__anchor__iUJ8y" target="" data-testid="link" rel="noreferrer" aria-label="Dr. Sakshi Sharma">Dr. Sakshi Sharma</a></span><span class="smallRegular">BDS</span></div></div><div class="marginTop-8 smallRegular textSecondary">Reviewed By<!-- --> <a href="https://www.1mg.com/editorial-policy-processes/dr.-varun-gupta-2" class="noAnchorColor ContentPageTitle__anchor__iUJ8y" target="" data-testid="link" rel="noreferrer" aria-label="Dr. Varun Gupta">Dr. Varun Gupta</a></div><div class="smallRegular">MD Pharmacology, MBBS</div><div class="marginTop-4 smallRegular textSecondary">Last updated on:<!-- --> <!-- -->27 Sep 2022 | 06:23 PM (IST)</div><div class="marginTop-16 bodyRegular textSecondary">Also known as hair fall, baldness, alopecia.</div></div></div><section class="Disease__overviewSection__OWBmx" id="overview"><div class="container-fluid widget-container"><div class="col-6 l4SemiBold marginTop-8">Overview</div><div class="col-6 marginTop-8 GeneralDescription__htmlNodeWrapper__h23K3 "><p dir="ltr">Generally, people shed around 50 to 100 single hair per day. Hair shedding is a natural process in which some hair sheds while new hair start to grow in. Hair loss or alopecia occurs when this balance is disrupted and more hair begin to fall than the new hair growing.</p>
<p dir="ltr"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p dir="ltr">Hair loss affects men, women, and sometimes even children. One may notice hair loss in the form of hair thinning, receding hairline, part widening, and bald patches. Age, genetics, nutritional deficiencies, hormonal imbalances, certain diseases and medications could be some of the causes of hair fall. However stress, tight hairstyles, chemical hair treatments and overuse of styling products, are also known to trigger hair fall.</p>
<p dir="ltr"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p dir="ltr">Hair loss does not have any harmful physical effects as such, but its psychological impact cannot be denied. For most people, their hair is inherently connected to their confidence. If their hair looks good, they feel good about themselves. But if they start losing hair, their self esteem begins to dwindle. In such a case, one can try one or many treatment options available for dealing with hair loss.</p>
<p dir="ltr"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p dir="ltr">Home remedies and oral hair supplements are usually the first line of action for hair loss. However, it is always advisable to visit a dermatologist or trichologist to get a proper diagnosis and treatment. Various treatment options include topical agents like Minoxidil, injections, oral treatments, Platelet rich plasma (PRP) therapy and hair transplantation.</p></div></div></section><section (min-width:769px){iframe.tinymceIframe{width:328px;height:200px}.tinymceImage{width:328px!important;height:auto!important}.tinymceButton{width:168px!important}}","description":"<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Definition of Hair Loss</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>Abnormal hair loss (alopecia) of more than 100 hairs a day is a cause of concern. Hair loss may be permanent or temporary, rapid or slow, and diffused, patterned or complete. It may be caused by genetic, environmental, or medical reasons and may or may not be treatable.</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Causes and Risk Factors of Hair Loss</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>When hair loss is permanent and accompanied with inflammation, skin problems, or tissue destruction, it is called scarring hair loss. There is no such scalp tissue damage in nonscarring hair loss.<br /><br /></div>\n<div>Androgenic alopecia is hair loss caused by genetic factors or family history. It is the common form of hair loss observed in both men and women where hair loss occurs in a certain pattern.</div>\n<div>Men usually start losing their hair above the temples and form a typical M shape, while thinning of hair all over the scalp is observed in women. It is more common in men, and usually occurs after menopause in women. Androgenic alopecia is caused by androgens, particularly dihydrotestosterone.</div>\n<div>Alopecia areata is a form of hair loss that occurs when body&rsquo;s immune system starts attacking healthy hair follicles. Hair loss occurs in well-rounded patches and may affect other body parts as well, including eyebrows and eyelashes.<br /><br /></div>\n<div>Alopecia areata may be caused by genetic or environmental factors or conditions such as celiac disease, vitiligo, atopy, and thyroid disorders. It affects both men and women, though is more commonly seen in males.<br /><br /></div>\n<div>Telogen effluvium is a rapid, sudden, diffuse hair loss that may be triggered by a disease, stressful situation, drugs, delivery, iron deficiency, weight loss, or fever. Hair loss may be severe with 100 to 200 hairs being shed daily. It is usually seen in women.</div>\n<div>Chronic telogen effluvium, seen in middle-aged women, is hair loss for more than 6 months accompanied with scalp pain.<br /><br /></div>\n<div>Traumatic alopecia is hair loss due to pulling or use of chemicals or heat (e.g., hair straightening).</div>\n<div>Trichotillomania is a form of hair loss that occurs due to repeated pulling and plucking of hair by the person itself. Patchy or irregular hair loss may occur without total baldness as small strands of hair remain on the scalp. It is a compulsive disorder and may require psychiatric help. It is more common in children.</div>\n<div>Other reasons that may trigger hair loss include:</div>\n<div>1. Poor nutrition</div>\n<div>2. Low protein diet</div>\n<div>3. Certain medicines</div>\n<div>4. Family history of hair loss</div>\n<div>5. Infections</div>\n<div>6. Chemotherapy for cancer (anagen effluvium)</div>\n<div>7. Autoimmune conditions such as allergic disorders, vitiligo, lupus, and rheumatoid arthritis</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Signs and Symptoms of Hair Loss</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>Abnormal hair loss occurs that may be mild (less than 100 hairs a day) or severe (100 to 200 hairs a day or more).</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Investigations</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>A detailed clinical examination along with family and medical history is required to determine the cause of hair loss. Physical exam to check pattern and extent of hair loss, inflammation or other skin issues, hirsutism or excess hair (in women) will be done.</div>\n<div>Pull test: The patient will be asked not to wash hair for 24 hours. About 60 hairs will be pulled gently. Out of them, six or more hair must get removed to suspect for excessive hair loss.</div>\n<div>1. Blood tests</div>\n<div>a) Complete blood count (CBC) to check for iron deficiency</div>\n<div>b) Thyroid stimulating hormone (TSH) for thyroid disorders</div>\n<div>c) ANA (antinuclear antibody) test</div>\n<div>d) RPR (rapid plasma regain) for syphilis</div>\n<div>2. Trichogram -- hair are visualized under light microscopy</div>\n<div>3. Scalp biopsy</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Treatment of Hair Loss</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>The treatment will depend on the extent of hair loss, the age of the patient, and the cause of hair loss. Treatment is more effective in mild cases of hair loss, though it may take months or years. Treatment may include one or more of the following:</div>\n<div>1. Finasteride and/or topical minoxidil for pattern alopecia in men</div>\n<div>2. Antiandrogens such as spironolactone or topical minoxidil for pattern alopecia (androgenic alopecia) in women</div>\n<div>3. Corticosteroid injections such as triamcinolone hexacetonide given once per month for alopecia areata</div>\n<div>4. Medicines such as methotrexate</div>\n<div>5. Topical immunotherapy</div>\n<div>If treatment does not work, hair transplantation may be considered. A hair weave (synthetic hair is sewn into existing hair) or a hair piece may help.</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Complications and When Should You See a Doctor</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>See a doctor if you have an abnormal rate of hair loss. Untreated hair loss may cause baldness.</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>Prognosis and Prevention</strong></div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div>If hair loss is caused due to a stress factor (traumatic alopecia, telogen effluvium), full regrowth of hair may occur once the stress factor is removed. Hair loss usually requires continuous medication and may relapse once the medicine is discontinued.</div>\n<div>&nbsp;</div>\n<div><strong>References</strong></div>\n<div>Skalecki J. Alopecia. Anagen phase </strong>is the active phase of hair growth that usually lasts for about two to six years. Around 85-90% of the hair on the scalp is in this stage at a given point in time.</p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong><br>2. Catagen phase</strong> is the transitional phase that lasts a few weeks (2-3 weeks). Only 1% of hair is in this stage.</p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><br><strong>3. Telogen phase</strong> is the end phase of hair growth, which is the resting phase. Around 13% of our hair is in this stage.</p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><br>At the end of the telogen phase, hair follicles are shed, which is replaced by new hair and the cycle continues. However, the hair growth cycle can be influenced by an individual’s age, diseases, hair care routine, and diet. </p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><br>Common causes of hair loss include:<br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Age:</strong> With age, it is common to notice some amount of hair fall. Men and women both notice receding hairline as well as thinning of hair.<br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Genetics:</strong> Hereditary causes are the most common cause of hair loss all over the world and both men and women are affected. It is also known as androgenic alopecia, male-pattern baldness and female-pattern baldness. It appears as a receding hairline and bald spots in men and thinning hair along the crown and a widening part in women.<br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Childbirth and other stressors:</strong> If you have recently given birth, or have had a chronic illness it can lead to hair fall. Stress or any kind of traumatic event may also trigger hair loss. <br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Ongoing treatment/medications:</strong> Certain undergoing treatment such as treatment for cancer, arthritis, depression, heart problems, gout and high blood pressure can trigger hair fall within a few days or weeks of starting the radiation or chemotherapy. <br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Tight hairstyles:</strong> Tight hairstyles such as braids can lead to hair fall over time. This is permanent hair loss and is known as traction alopecia. <br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Scalp infections:</strong> A scalp infection, which appears as scaly and inflamed results in hair loss. <br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Hormonal imbalance: </strong>Certain women experience hair loss due to hormonal imbalances in conditions such as PCOS (polycystic ovarian syndrome). Birth control pills, which are hormonal preparations, can also trigger hair fall.<br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Nutritional deficiencies:</strong> If your diet lacks protein, zinc, biotin, iron or any other essential nutrient then you may notice hair fall and thinning of hair. <br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Disease:</strong> Diseases such as hyperthyroidism, hypothyroidism, diabetes, lupus and STI’s (sexually transmitted infections) can lead to hair fall as well as bald patches on the eyebrows, lashes, and other parts of the body.<br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Pulling your own hair: </strong>Also known as Trichotillomania, it is the habit of pulling one’s own hair that may lead to permanent hair loss over time. </p>","isSeparator":true,"identifier":"causes"},{"wType":"freeText","content":"<h2>Symptoms Of Hair Loss<br><br>\n</h2>\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Signs and symptoms of hair loss can present in many ways as the following:</p>\n<ul>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Gradual loss or thinning of hair on top of head.</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<ul>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Receding hairline(frontal fibrosing alopecia). If the hairline starts looking higher than the usual position.</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<ul>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Widening partition. If someone parts their hair, they might notice the part getting wider over time.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Circular or bald patches. Some people develop circular or bald patches on their scalp, beard or eyebrows.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Loosening  of hair. Clumps of hair might come out while combing or washing hair.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Thinner ponytail.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Scalp starts getting visible through the hair.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Full-body hair loss. Some health conditions and treatments such as chemotherapy for cancer, can cause loss of hair from all over the body.</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><br>Hair loss can be gradual or rapid. The symptoms for gradual hair loss include hair thinning, widening of part, receding hairline. The symptoms for rapid hair loss include clumps of hair in comb or drain, a bald patch that appeared recently and severe hair fall.</p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><br><em><strong>Note: Gradual hair loss is more common and tends to affect everybody at least once in their lifetime. The signs of gradual hair loss are subtle and may take a long time before you even notice your hair fall!</strong></em></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><br>Apart from the obvious signs of hair fall, some other symptoms may also be present with your hair fall. </p>\n<ul>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Intense itching and redness in the scalp: </strong>This could occur due to an underlying infection in the scalp.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Scaly bald patches, often with sores:</strong> It can be a sign of fungal infection like ringworm or due to a chronic disease like psoriasis. </p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Burning and tingling on the scalp:</strong> Some people who have alopecia areata experience might experience burning and stinging prior to sudden hair loss.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Pus-filled sores on the scalp: </strong>Some conditions such as folliculitis can cause pus-filled blisters on the scalp resulting in temporary hair loss.</p>\n</li>\n</ul>","isSeparator":true,"identifier":"symptoms"},{"wType":"freeText","content":"<h2>Types Of Hair Loss<br><br>\n</h2>\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Hair loss, also known as alopecia, is broadly classified into cicatricial alopecia and non-cicatricial alopecia. In non-cicatricial alopecia, hair loss is not permanent whereas in cicatricial alopecia, scars occur along with hair fall and destroy the hair follicle resulting in permanent hair loss. A few types of hair loss are discussed below:<br><br></p>\n<h3 dir=\"ltr\"><strong>1. Non-cicatricial or Non-scarring alopecia</strong></h3>\n<ul>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Androgenic alopecia:</strong> Androgenic alopecia is also called hereditary hair loss. In men, it is known as male pattern baldness which is characterised by gradual loss of hair above the temples and thinning at the top of the head, usually creating a shape of ‘M’. In women, it is known as the female pattern baldness and results in thinning all over the scalp or widening of the part.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Alopecia areata:</strong>  It is an autoimmune disorder in which the body starts to attack its own hair follicles. This is hair loss that can affect every part of the body, including the scalp, face, trunk, and extremities. When it affects only a portion of the body, it is called alopecia areata. When it affects an entire site it is called alopecia totalis. When it involves the whole body, it is called alopecia universalis which is mostly associated with conditions like vitiligo and thyroid disorders. </p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Anagen effluvium:</strong> In this, diffuse and rapid hair loss occurs, which is mainly caused by the effect of radiation and chemotherapy. Hair usually grow back after completion of the treatment.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Telogen effluvium: </strong>It is a type of sudden diffuse hair fall that is mostly seen after some stressful event, period of emotional shock , illnesses or taking certain medications. It can also occur due to hormonal fluctuations that happen in pregnancy, childbirth, starting or stopping hormonal birth control pills or menopause.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Traction alopecia:</strong> This type of alopecia results from too much pressure on the hair, mostly because of tight braids, ponytails, or buns.</p>\n</li>\n<li dir=\"ltr\" style=\"list-style-type: disc;\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>Trichotillomania: </strong>In this type of impulse control disorder, a person pulls his/her own hair subconsciously. This leads to irregular bald patches and uneven hair length. It mostly occurs in children or adolescents. In children, it is more like a habit that will eventually resolve on its own, but in adolescents, psychiatric help might be required.</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3 dir=\"ltr\">\n<br><strong>2. Cicatricial alopecia or scarring alopecia<br><br></strong>\n</h3>\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Cicatricial alopecia is a broad umbrella encompassing uncommon inflammatory hair loss disorders that result in scarring patches of hair loss with absence of hair follicles. Causes of hair follicle destruction include fungal infections, chemicals such as hair relaxers, and inflammatory disorders which include discoid lupus erythematosus, lichen planopilaris, dissecting cellulitis, tufted folliculitis, folliculitis decalvans, alopecia mucinosa, alopecia neoplastica, central centrifugal cicatricial alopecia, and acne keloidalis.</p>","isSeparator":true,"identifier":"types"},{"actionLabel":"Read More About COVID-19!","image":"https://onemg.gumlet.io/a_ignore,w_360,c_fit,q_auto,f_auto/sw3hthgyidoaoifdihoo.svg","redirectionUrl":"https://www.1mg.com/coronavirus-covid19?utm_medium=Hair%20loss_low_emphasis_choice_4&utm_source=disease_page","isSeparator":true,"header":"I have recovered from COVID-19. Why am I facing hair loss?\n\n","wType":"lowEmphasisChoice","description":"While most people think they are suffering from hair loss after recovering from COVID-19, it is actually hair shedding. It is called Telogen Effluvium and usually occurs around 3 months after a stressful event. A fever or illness like COVID-19 can force more hair to enter the shedding (telogen) phase of the hair growth life cycle at the same time. Most people see that their hair starts looking normal and stops shedding after 6 to 9 months.\n\n"},{"wType":"freeText","content":"<h2>Risk Factors For Hair Loss<br><br>\n</h2>\n<p dir=\"ltr\">There are many risk factors for developing hair loss. Some of these risk factors can be avoided, while others cannot. Other diagnostic measures include a fungal screening of the scalp, hair pull, and tug test, and light microscopy, and/or trichoscopy.<br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>1. Pull test:</strong> In this test, also known as traction test, 20-60 hair strands are grasped between your thumb and index and middle finger, held from the hair shaft firmly, and tugged away from the scalp. If the hair shedding is more than 10% of the total hair grasped then it is called a ‘positive pull test’ &amp; indicates active hair shedding. </p>\n<br>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>2. Light microscopic examination:</strong> The hair that is collected by the pull tests is then examined under the microscope for fractures, irregularities, coiling, and other hair shaft disorders. </p>\n<br>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>3. Scalp biopsy: </strong>Scalp biopsies are done in cases of cicatricial hair loss and undiagnosed cases of non-cicatricial alopecia. <br><br><strong>4. Also, sometimes doctors may recommend blood tests to check the level of various nutrients as deficiencies of these can lead to hair loss. The following are usually tested:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<strong>Iron:</strong> Iron deficiency in pre-menopausal women is one the major causes of hair loss. Iron contributes to hemoglobin production, which helps in delivering nutrients and oxygen to hair follicles. When iron is not present in adequate amounts the hair won’t grow, causing progressively thinner hair. </li>\n<li>\n<strong>Zinc:</strong> Zinc deficiency can also impact hair growth and cause hair thinning.</li>\n<li>\n<strong>Biotin:</strong> Also known as Vitamin B7, it stimulates keratin production in hair and can increase follicle growth. The scarring left behind on the donor site is covered up with new hair. This technique requires much aftercare and is quite a hassle to go through. <br><br></p>\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><strong>2.                     // if (typeof window.SERVICE_WORKER_REGISTRATION !== "undefined") {
                    //     window.SERVICE_WORKER_REGISTRATION.unregister();

                    // Service worker disabled due to issues with Cloudflare CDN (sw was not getting new assets from cdn on new deployment)
                    (async function main() {
                        const deploymentPlatform = "mweb";
                        if (deploymentPlatform === "dweb") return;
                        const env = "production";
                        if ("serviceWorker" in navigator) {
                            if (env === "production") {
                                navigator.serviceWorker
                                    .register("/pwa-api/service-worker.js", { scope: "/" })
                                    .then(registration => {
                                        console.info("Service Worker is registered!");
                                        window.SERVICE_WORKER_REGISTRATION = registration;
                                    });

                                //Triggers when user installs the application
                                window.addEventListener("appinstalled", (e) => {
                                    if (window.rudderanalytics && window.rudderanalytics.track) {
                                        window.rudderanalytics.track("Install Event", {
                                            category: "PWA Installed",
                                            label: "PWA APP Installed",
                                        })
                                    }
                                })
                            }
                        }
                        else {
                            console.log(
                                "Service Worker is not supported in your browser"
                            );
                        }

                        //Triggers when the PWA is already installed on system
                        if ('getInstalledRelatedApps' in navigator) {
                            const installedApps = await navigator.getInstalledRelatedApps();
                            const PWAisInstalled = installedApps.length > 0;
                            console.log("Is PWA already installed on the system?", PWAisInstalled, installedApps)
                            if (PWAisInstalled) {
                                if (window.rudderanalytics && window.rudderanalytics.track) {
                                    window.rudderanalytics.track("PWA Already Installed Event", {
                                        category: "PWA Installed",
                                        label: "PWA Already Installed",
                                    })
                                }
                            }
                        }
                        //Triggers if PWA is launched in Standalone mode
                        if (window.matchMedia('(display-mode: standalone)').matches) {
                            if (window.rudderanalytics && window.rudderanalytics.track) {
                                window.rudderanalytics.track("Launch Event", {
                                    category: "PWA Launched",
                                    label: "PWA Launched Standalone",
                                })
                            }
                        }
                    })();


                </script>
